<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

	<div class="pure-g">
		<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.impactStatement || vm.details.abstract || vm.details.scope || vm.details.purpose  || vm.details.previewImage --><div ng-if="::vm.details.impactStatement || vm.details.abstract || vm.details.scope || vm.details.purpose  || vm.details.previewImage" ng-class="vm.details.graphicalAbstract ? 		<!--div ng-class="{'pure-u-14-24 u-pr-1':  vm.details.graphicalAbstract, 'pure-u-1-1': ! vm.details.graphicalAbstract}"-->
			<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.abstract --><div ng-if="::vm.details.abstract" class="ng-scope">
				<strong>Abstract:</strong>
				<div class="abstract-text ng-binding" ng-bind-html="::vm.details.abstract">The passive UHF RFID technology, well known for the logistics and security applications, is more and more considered for sensor networks and Internet of Things (IoT). Recent works have demonstrated the possibility to exploit the main advantages of RFID in the millimeter-wave domain, giving rise to the millimeter wave identification (MMID) technology. This new technology uses the large available ISM band from 57 to 66 GHz in Europe. In backscatter communications, such as RFID or MMID, the radar cross section (RCS) is a fundamental parameter. The antenna RCS is defined as a function of its load and its structural coefficient. The structural coefficient that depends on the antenna geometry is often approximated to unity in RFID because tag antennas are usually thin dipoles compared to the wavelength. However, in MMID this approximation is no longer suitable due to the use of high directive antennas. This letter aims to propose a method to determine the structural coefficient of any types of antenna. The proposed approach is illustrated through the study of a horn antenna and a slotted waveguide antenna array in WR15 waveguide (from 50 to 75 GHz). Theoretical, simulation, and measurement results are compared and demonstrate the interest of the method.</div>
			</div><!-- end ngIf: ::vm.details.abstract -->			
			<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.scope -->
			<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.purpose -->
		</div><!-- end ngIf: ::vm.details.impactStatement || vm.details.abstract || vm.details.scope || vm.details.purpose  || vm.details.previewImage -->

<div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>The passive ultra high frequency (UHF) radio frequency identification (RFID) technology has been widely deployed in logistics and security applications, and actually is evolving for sensor networks and Internet of Things (IoT) paradigm <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>. The advantages of this technology rely on the use of backscatter communications where the tag responds to the reader by modulating its radar cross section (RCS) and the remote power supply. With the opening of 9 GHz of unlicensed band from 57 to 66 GHz in Europe <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>, the millimeter wave identification (MMID) becomes a very attractive topic for dense wireless networks requiring energy-efficient and high throughput <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a>.</p><p>The RCS is the fundamental parameter in backscatter communications. The RCS of a loaded antenna depends both on the antenna geometry and the load. It is defined as a function of the complex structural coefficient and the reflection coefficient between the antenna and the load. Usually in UHF RFID, the structural coefficient is approximated to unity because tag antennas are half-wavelength dipole-like antennas, whose thickness is negligible compared to the wavelength <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a>. In MMID, tags are usually directive in order to compensate the propagation losses <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a> and, as a consequence, the previous assumption is no longer valid. The use of the theoretical expression of the RCS, for instance in order to ensure the optimal conditions for backscattering communications, requires the determination of the structural coefficient.</p><p>Different methods exist to quantify the structural mode and the antenna mode in terms of RCS <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a>. However, these methods do not calculate the structural coefficient of the antenna. A graphical methodology, based on Green's analysis on scattering antennas, is used to determine the structural coefficient of a large RFID tag antenna <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_1">[9]</a>. However, this method is not suitable for a broadband characterization in the millimeter-wave domain.</p><p>This work presents a method to determine the complex structural coefficient of any types of antenna. <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec2" class="fulltext-link">Section II</a> presents the analytical model of the loaded antenna RCS and highlights the fundamental critical points when dealing with MMID tag antenna. <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3" class="fulltext-link">Section III</a> presents the proposed approach to calculate the complex structural coefficient. An algorithm of correction of the measurement or simulation errors is also highlighted. <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec4" class="fulltext-link">Section IV</a> validates the proposed method by calculating the structural coefficient of two antennas in the band 57–66 GHz. <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec5" class="fulltext-link">Section V</a> presents the final conclusions and perspectives.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Theory on Loaded Antenna Radar Cross Section</h2></div><p>An antenna illuminated by a plane wave scatters the incoming field in function of its RCS. For a loaded antenna, the backscattered field is composed by two components. One component, called the structural mode, only depends on the antenna geometry. The other component, called the antenna mode, depends on the load connected to the antenna <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_2">[5]</a>. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a> illustrates the two components of the backscattered wave.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig1"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7398195/7123576/7123576-fig-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7398195/7123576/7123576-fig-1-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 1. </b><fig><p>Two components of the backscattered wave <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-1-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1" role="math" style="width: 3.442em; <p></p><p>These two modes are directly related to the definition of the total RCS of the loaded antenna, expressed by <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_2">[5]</a> <disp-formula id="deqn1" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><div class="MathJax_Display"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-4-Frame" tabindex="0" style="width: 100%;"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-30" role="math" style="width: 100%; However, if the transmission line and the load are also illuminated by the incident plane wave, their physical structure will reflect some power, and so the coefficient <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-9-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-127" role="math" style="width: 2.946em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.646em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1002.65em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-128"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-129"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-130"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-131"><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-133"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-134"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-135" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">s</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-136" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-137" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">r</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-138" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">u</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-139" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">c</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-140" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-9">{A_{\rm struct}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> will also take into account these effects. As introduced in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec1" class="fulltext-link">Section I</a>, it is worth noticing that in passive UHF RFID, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-10-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-141" role="math" style="width: 2.946em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.646em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1002.65em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-142"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-143"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-144"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-145"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.646em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-146" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">A</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-147"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-148"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-149" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">s</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-150" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-151" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">r</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-152" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">u</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-153" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">c</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-154" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-10">{A_{\rm struct}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is approximated to unity; approximation is however not suitable for MMID antennas that are usually directive antennad. For backscatter communications, one of the main objectives of the tag design is the maximization of the backscattered level to enhance the communication range <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_2">[10]</a>. In the MMID context, the requirement of an accurate value of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-11-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-155" role="math" style="width: 2.946em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.646em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1002.65em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-156"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-157"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-158"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-159"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.646em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-160" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">A</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-161"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-162"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-163" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">s</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-164" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-165" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">r</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-166" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">u</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-167" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">c</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-168" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; <div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Determination of the Complex Structural Coefficient</h2></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3a"><h3>A. Determination of the Reflection Coefficient</h3><p>Classic RFID and MMID tags are composed by an antenna, an integrated chip (IC), and a transmission line that connects the chip to the antenna. In UHF RFID, the propagation line is usually not included in the electrical model because of its short length compared to the wavelength <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_3a">[8]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_3a">[9]</a>, whereas in millimeter waves, the transmission line has to be taken into account in the model.</p><p>The electrical model of an MMID tag is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2</a>. The load of impedance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-13-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-201" role="math" style="width: 1.444em; font-family: MathJax_Main;">s</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-633" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-634" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">r</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-635" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">u</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-636" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">c</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-637" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-38">{A_{\rm struct}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> exists physically. Thus, the third one permits to select the unique physical solution for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-39-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-638" role="math" style="width: 0.604em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.544em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.54em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-639"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-640" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">a</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.67em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-39">a</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-40-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-641" role="math" style="width: 0.483em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.423em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.42em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-642"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-643" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">b</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-40">b</script></tex-math></inline-formula> among the two mathematical possible solutions.

<p></p><p>Finally, as all the parameters in <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn4" href="#deqn4" class="fulltext-link">(4)</a> are defined in function of the frequency, the proposed approach allows the complete determination of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-43-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-658" role="math" style="width: 2.946em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.646em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1002.65em 2.526em -999.997em); font-family: MathJax_Main;">r</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-669" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">u</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-670" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">c</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-671" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; Practical Considerations</h3><p>
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig4"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7398195/7123576/7123576-fig-4-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7398195/7123576/7123576-fig-4-small.gif" alt="Figure 4" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 4. </b><fig><p>Approximated solution <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-44-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-672" role="math" style="width: 5.691em; In practice, due to measurement errors or simulation inaccuracy, it is possible to have cases where there is no solution because the circles are disjoint (even if close to each other). In order to solve this issue (if it exists), a possible approach is to determine an approximated solution <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-47-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-731" role="math" style="width: 5.168em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.628em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.51em 2.706em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-732"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-733" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-734"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-735"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-736"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-737"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-738"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.745em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1000.48em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-739" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">a</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.544em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-740"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-741"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-742" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">a</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-743" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">p</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-744" style="font-size: 70.7%; <div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Examples of Structural Coefficient Calculation</h2></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4a"><h3>A Presentation of Antennas Under Test and Considered Loads</h3><p>In order to illustrate the proposed method, the structural coefficients of two different antennas are calculated. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5</a> shows the antennas under test (AUTs) and the considered loads <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-54-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-806" role="math" style="width: 1.444em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.264em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.26em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-807"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-808"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-809"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-810"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.264em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-811" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-812" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-54">{Z_L}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The first AUT [<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5(a)</a>] is a V-band linearly polarized horn antenna of aperture <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-55-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-813" role="math" style="width: 6.249em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.589em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.204em 1005.59em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-814"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-815" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">21</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-816" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">×</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-817" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">18</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-818" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-819"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.105em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1001.68em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-820"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-821"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-822" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.381em; left: 1.685em;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-823" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-55">21 \times 18~\hbox{mm}^2</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The second AUT [<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5(b)</a>] is the slotted waveguide antenna array (SWAA) introduced in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_4a">[11]</a>, of aperture <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-56-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-824" role="math" style="width: 7.931em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 7.15em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.204em 1007.15em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-825"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-826" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">26.5</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-827" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">×</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-828" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">8.16</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-829" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-830"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.105em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1001.68em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-831"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-832"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-833" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">mm</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.381em; left: 1.685em;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-834" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-56">26.5 \times 8.16~\hbox{mm}^2</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. In the 57–66 GHz band, the horn antenna presents a realized gain from 20.6 to 21.5 dBi, while the SWAA realized gain is from −3.2 to 10.7 dBi. The antennas are chosen for their 3-D complex structures, WR15 waveguide connection, and the coverage of a wide band of gain values (from −3.2 to 21.5 dBi). As both antennas are linearly polarized with a gain in cross polarization that is at minimum 100 dB lower than in copolarization, the study is performed only in copolarization.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig5"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7398195/7123576/7123576-fig-5-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7398195/7123576/7123576-fig-5-small.gif" alt="Figure 5" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 5. </b><fig><p>Photographs of the AUT and the loads. (a) horn antenna. (b) swaa. (c) wr15 waveguide. (d) short-circuit plate. (e) matched load.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7123576/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>The chosen loads, connected to the antennas through a WR15 waveguide of length 25.4 mm [<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5(c)</a>], are the short-circuit (SC) with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-57-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-835" role="math" style="width: 3.547em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.186em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1003.13em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-836"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-837"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-838"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-839"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-840" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-841"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-842"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-843" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">s</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-844" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">c</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-845" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-846" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">0</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-57">{Z_{\rm sc}} = 0</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the matched load (ML) with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-58-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-847" role="math" style="width: 4.508em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.027em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1004.03em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-848"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-849"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-850"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-851"><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-853"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-854"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-855" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-856" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">l</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-857" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-858" style="padding-left: 0.303em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-859"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-860"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-861" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-862" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">c</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-58">{Z_{\rm ml}} = {Z_c}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and the open waveguide (OW) with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-59-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-863" role="math" style="width: 1.805em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.625em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.63em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-864"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-865"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-866"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-867"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.625em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-868" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-869"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-870"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-871" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">o</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-872" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">w</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-59">{Z_{\rm ow}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> varying in function of the frequency. The SC is reached by ending the waveguide with a short-circuit plate [<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5(d)</a>], while the OW consists on leaving the waveguide end open. In the case of the OW, as the waveguide impedance (around 500<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-60-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-873" role="math" style="width: 1.084em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.9em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-874"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-875" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-876" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-60">~\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>) is near to the vacuum impedance (377<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-61-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-877" role="math" style="width: 1.084em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.9em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-878"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-879" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-880" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-61">~\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>), the OW impedance is not infinite (contrary to the open circuit) and must be determined by simulation or measurement. For example, the simulated impedance at 60 GHz is <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-62-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-881" role="math" style="width: 9.372em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 8.411em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1008.35em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-882"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-883"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-884"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-885"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.625em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-886" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">Z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-887"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-888"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-889" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">o</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-890" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">w</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-891" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-892" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">486</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-893" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">−</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-894" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic; padding-left: 0.243em;">j</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-895" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">200</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-896" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-62">{Z_{\rm ow}} = 486 - j200\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Finally, for each frequency in the computation, the associated value of the OW impedance is used.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4b"><h3>B Practical Considerations To Apply the Method</h3><p>The calculation of the complex structural coefficient based on the exposed method relies on the primarily determination of the following:

The RCS measurement is realized with a monostatic configuration as presented in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_4b">[12]</a>. In the measurement setup, the transmitting/receiving antenna is the same horn antenna shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5(a)</a>. The <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-74-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-987" role="math" style="width: 0.724em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.664em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.66em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-988"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-989" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-74">S</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-parameters are acquired by the Agilent N5222A VNA and a Virginia Diodes WR15-VNAX 50–75 GHz VNA extension. A time-gating procedure is used to extract the AUT response from the environment.</p><p>Finally, the calculation of the complex structural coefficient <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-75-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-990" role="math" style="width: 2.946em; top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-991"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-992"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-993"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-994"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.646em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-995" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">A</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-996"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-997"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-998" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">s</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-999" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1000" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">r</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1001" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">u</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1002" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">c</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1003" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-75">{A_{\rm struct}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is performed by numerical computation from 57 to 66 GHz with a frequency step of 12.5 MHz following the described method, including the introduced correction algorithm. In order to match all the simulated and the measured results, it is worth noticing that the simulations and measurements are processed in the same frequency band with the same frequency step.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4c"><h3>C Results</h3><p>

Both results are in good agreement. For example, from 63.9 to 64.1 GHz in the case of the horn antenna and from 60.9 to 61.6 GHz in the case of the SWAA, the correction algorithm is carried out and leads to consistent results. Otherwise, as expected, it is clear that the classic approximation in UHF RFID, i.e., <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-87-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1174" role="math" style="width: 5.048em; <p></p><p>The RCS calculated with the reinjected <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-91-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1232" role="math" style="width: 2.946em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.646em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1002.65em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1233"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1234"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1235"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1236"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.646em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1237" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">A</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1238"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1239"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1240" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">s</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1241" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1242" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">r</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1243" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">u</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1244" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">c</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1245" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-91">{A_{\rm struct}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is in good agreement with the full-wave simulated RCS for each case, validating the proposed method (algorithm of correction included) to calculate the structural coefficient.</p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec5"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION V.</div><h2>Conclusion</h2></div><p>In this letter, a method to determine the complex structural coefficient in function of the frequency of any antenna, whatever the considered frequency band, is presented. The method relies on the mathematical definition of the RCS introducing the resolution of an equations system whose unknowns are the real and imaginary parts of the structural coefficient. The approach requires the prior knowledge of the gain and the impedance of the considered antenna and the RCS of three different loads. As indeterminate cases can appear because of approximations related to the RCS acquisition, a correction algorithm associated to the method is also introduced. The method is illustrated by considering two antennas, a horn antenna and an SWAA, from 57 to 66 GHz, using three loads: a short circuit, a matched load, and an open waveguide, but any other loads could be suitable. As a first result, the knowledge of the structural coefficient permits to easily calculate the RCS for any type of load. In perspectives, the proposed method is also relevant for the optimization procedure of new backscattering communications such as MMID, where the calculation of the structural coefficient permits to find the optimal load that maximize the RCS of the tag, increasing the read range <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_5">[10]</a>.</p></div>
</div></div>

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

	{
		if(IBP_WS_ENABLED_FLAG){
		Modal.refreshLegacyAccountTransition('/xpl/mwLegacyAccountTransition.jsp');
		}
	}
});

</script>

Recent works have demonstrated the possibility to exploit the main advantages of RFID in the millimeter-wave domain, giving rise to the millimeter wave identification (MMID) technology. This new technology uses the large available ISM band from 57 to 66 GHz in Europe. In backscatter communications, such as RFID or MMID, the radar cross section (RCS) is a fundamental parameter. The antenna RCS is defined as a function of its load and its structural coefficient. The structural coefficient that depends on the antenna geometry is often approximated to unity in RFID because tag antennas are usually thin dipoles compared to the wavelength. However, in MMID this approximation is no longer suitable due to the use of high directive antennas. This letter aims to propose a method to determine the structural coefficient of any types of antenna. The proposed approach is illustrated through the study of a horn antenna and a slotted waveguide antenna array in WR15 waveguide (from 50 to 75 GHz). Theoretical, simulation, and measurement results are compared and demonstrate the interest of the method.","keywords":[{"type":"IEEE Keywords","kwd":["Loaded antennas","Antenna
